<div id="review_341598421" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/341598421" />
    <a title="Jane Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart"><img alt="Jane Stewart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346001994p2/3789528.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/341598421?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane Stewart" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart">Jane Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10289899-providence">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=young-adult-paranormal-romance">young-adult-paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer341598421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15238750497475618075">It wasn’t interesting enough. I wanted it to be over. Annoying heroine stupidity.<br/><br/>PARANORMAL SET-UP:<br/>It wasn’t made clear, but I believe a small number of people in the world have a protector-guardian angel. Jack was wealthy and had many enemies. Gabe was Jack’s guardian angel. Gabe was like a secret agent with super powers. When Jack is killed in a car accident, Gabe died shortly after. Angels die when their taleh (their protectee) dies. Previously, Gabe married a human Lillian. They had three ch</span>
  <span id="freeText15238750497475618075" style="display:none">It wasn’t interesting enough. I wanted it to be over. Annoying heroine stupidity.<br /><br />PARANORMAL SET-UP:<br />It wasn’t made clear, but I believe a small number of people in the world have a protector-guardian angel. Jack was wealthy and had many enemies. Gabe was Jack’s guardian angel. Gabe was like a secret agent with super powers. When Jack is killed in a car accident, Gabe died shortly after. Angels die when their taleh (their protectee) dies. Previously, Gabe married a human Lillian. They had three children who have angel powers Jared, Claire, and Bex. Angels have no choice in who their taleh is. When they see them they know. They also know they will die when their taleh dies. The angel feels the pains and emotions that their taleh feels.<br /><br />Jack had one daughter Nina. Nina is Jared’s taleh. For years Jared has been secretly watching her as a protector. He has hidden cameras and microphones in places she lives and in her car. Jack paid a salary to Gabe and Jared for their protective services to him and his daughter. After Jack dies, his estate continues to pay Jared to protect Nina. (Summary: Guardian angels exist but they need to be paid a salary for their services. Question: If the taleh is poor, who pays for the salary and surveillance equipment?) Other characters are demons from hell and archangels who are more powerful than regular angels.<br /><br />The story begins when Nina meets Jared for the first time after her father’s funeral. <br /><br />REVIEWER’S OPINION:<br />The setting involves angels, but one could write the same story without angels - have Jared work in the security business and be good at shooting and fighting. The plot is: boy is hired to protect girl. He falls in love with her but must stay away so he can protect her better. She falls in love with him at first sight. She wants to know his secrets. Bad guys threaten girl.<br /><br />The above set-up is ok, but I was expecting more about the angel-demon world. There is only one brief scene with a demon. The first half was ok because I was curious. But during the last half I wanted it to be over. I was skimming parts to get to the good stuff and main events. And then, heroine stupidity made it worse.<br /><br />HEROINE STUPIDITY:<br />I was annoyed when she broke up with Jared for a stupid and illogical reason. It was one of those I love you but I’m staying away from you for your own good even though we will both be miserable. Also without your protection, I will probably be killed. I was further annoyed when the heroine did something else stupid while they were apart.<br /><br />The author has good writing skills. When I was giving constructive criticism to another author, I used Jamie McGuire as an example of how to write a conversation scene without saying hi, how are you, and goodbye. <br /><br />THE SERIES:<br />Nina and Jared continue as the main characters in the two sequels “Requiem” and “Eden.”<br /><br />DATA:<br />Kindle count story length: 11,440 (707 KB). Swearing language: mild, including religious swear words. Sexual content: Sex occurred one time but no details were shown. Setting: current day Providence, Rhode Island, and a small island off the coast of Nicaragua. Copyright: 2010. Genre: young adult paranormal romance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15238750497475618075" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_346682669" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/346682669" />
    <a title="Lis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3378688-lis"><img alt="Lis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469205616p2/3378688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/346682669?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lis" href="/user/show/3378688-lis">Lis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3378688-lis?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3378688-lis?shelf=cliffhanger-anyone-anyone">cliffhanger-anyone-anyone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3378688-lis?shelf=angels-and-other-things-involving-w">angels-and-other-things-involving-w</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3378688-lis?shelf=scary-but-not-for-normal-reasons">scary-but-not-for-normal-reasons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3378688-lis?shelf=laugh-out-loud-as-in-lol">laugh-out-loud-as-in-lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3378688-lis?shelf=this-made-me-blushhhh">this-made-me-blushhhh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer346682669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9318929694412957922">Also Found On: <a href='http://abookandarecord.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Book and A Record</a><br/><br/>Let me start by saying that one of my goodreads friends (Cindy over at Once Upon a Time Book Reviews – click our link to her site, she’s great!) was really excited about this book, and though my TBR list on my Kindle is hovering somewhere around 110 titles, I knew that this one was going get pushed to the top. I’m so glad that it did! So thank you, Cindy, for getting so excited about such a fun read!<br/>Providence is a really amazing blend that has slight elements o</span>
  <span id="freeText9318929694412957922" style="display:none">Also Found On: <a href="http://abookandarecord.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">A Book and A Record</a><br /><br />Let me start by saying that one of my goodreads friends (Cindy over at Once Upon a Time Book Reviews – click our link to her site, she’s great!) was really excited about this book, and though my TBR list on my Kindle is hovering somewhere around 110 titles, I knew that this one was going get pushed to the top. I’m so glad that it did! So thank you, Cindy, for getting so excited about such a fun read!<br />Providence is a really amazing blend that has slight elements of the Twilight novels and the Hush, Hush saga, however it is unique. Here is why:<br />1. Jared. Jared’s love for Nina has been growing for quite some time. He doesn’t see her across the lunch room, he purposefully inserts himself into her life with every intention of staying there. This isn’t a “hey look at the hot girl over there, I can’t live without her.” It’s built upon things in the past (cue: the diary-reading scene, melt my heart!) Although Jared is overprotective, I felt that he had a legitimate, tried and true, had already taken 1 bullet for this girl, reason to be overprotective. He also wasn’t afraid to admit that his weakness was if anything happened to her. Both literally and figuratively.<br />2. The Setting: Seriously. This setting works so perfectly for this type of story and I felt like it played really well into helping move the story forward. You know how is Harry Potter, J.K. Rowling is always giving hints about what is to come through the way the weather is acting? That’s kind of what McGuire does in Providence, I love when weather and setting is incorporated into a story. And I love when a story is set on a Uni campus! I feel like it encourages readers to head to University, which I wholeheartedly support.<br />3. The Story. I will be the first to admit that I am a sucker for the stories that are like this one. Although I haven’t made my way through the Twilight books recently, they do have a very fond place in my heart. Not only because they really propelled me into a wider variety of paranormal books, but because they boosted the YA industry into what it is today. That being said: I love stories about true love! I love stories that have a happy ending! I love stories that are entertaining and fun to read. Providence is that way for me. It was fun, it was light (material wise), and a great one to curl up on the couch and read over an afternoon. <br />I’ll admit: The only thing I didn’t like about this book was Ryan. Ryan was annoying. I felt like through the entire book he was pushing himself onto Nina, and although I think there was something (on the authors part) to turn Ryan/Nina/Jared into a love-triangle, I honestly never felt like Ryan stood a chance. I mean seriously? He was annoying and so cocky it made me was to hurl. <br />Holy crap guys I give this with a warning: this book with suck you in. I’ve joked before, but this one really felt like I had gone down the rabbit hole and wouldn’t be coming back out for a while. I can’t wait to get started on the sequel! I’m giving it four pies, because I am literally hungry for more! Requiem here I come! </span>
  <a data-text-id="9318929694412957922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15702445181973538564">I am honestly confused by the high praise for this book! Having never read 'Beautiful Disaster', I had no expectations for this book. It turns out that somehow, this book cannot even beat my complete lack of expectation (which is truly saying something, because I have read some horrendous YA fiction in my time)<br/><br/>From what I have read of this book (I could only tolerate 1/3 of the book until I couldn't stand it anymore), it's full of what I dislike about YA fiction.<br/><br/><b>1. A boring protagonist</b><br/>Meet Nina,</span>
  <span id="freeText15702445181973538564" style="display:none">I am honestly confused by the high praise for this book! Having never read 'Beautiful Disaster', I had no expectations for this book. It turns out that somehow, this book cannot even beat my complete lack of expectation (which is truly saying something, because I have read some horrendous YA fiction in my time)<br /><br />From what I have read of this book (I could only tolerate 1/3 of the book until I couldn't stand it anymore), it's full of what I dislike about YA fiction.<br /><br /><b>1. A boring protagonist</b><br />Meet Nina, aka the boring protagonist. I'm not looking for a girl with superhero powers or an alien from outer space. All I'm asking for is a non Mary-Sue who is genuinely likeable. I can find very few redeeming features of our girl Nina (who everyone loves for some reason completely unbeknownst to me...) - especially when she calls her BMW a Beemer.<br /><br /><b>2. Creepiness disguised as being romantic.</b><br />Being in love with a girl who you've watched grow up while she is unaware of your presence or infatuation is not cute. At all. If Nina had any sense at all, she'd slap a restraining order on him.<br /><br /><b>3. S...l.......o......w....</b><br />I got the one third point in the book and NOTHING HAS HAPPENED. There is not even anything to make me want to continue reading (Not the answers of what was Nina's dad really up to, or what does Ryel really do - I was so bored at this stage that I didn't care to find out)<br /><br /><b>4. General ridiculous things that make me cringe</b> <br />"Jared made a strange face as if he didn't know how to react to my little anecdote, and then returned to the kitchen. He brought out a bowl of steamed vegetables, a plate of dinner rolls, and a baked potato... all of them favourites of mine" (p.95)<br /><br />(I KID YOU NOT. THIS WAS ACTUALLY IN THE BOOK.)<br /><br />Yes of course those are your favourites Nina. Because they are bland just like your personality.<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6351205927282161941">Ok I have to be honest. I started this book with some pretty high expectations. I was looking for another Beautiful Disaster. But part way through the book i realized I didn't want another BD, not really. I wanted a book that would provoke the same feelings BD did. I can't say this book did that exactly, but it was still a great book. In fact I would have loved it more had I not been comparing it to BD so much I think.<br/><br/>OK enough babbling, I loved it. I read reviews before reading it and so some o</span>
  <span id="freeText6351205927282161941" style="display:none">Ok I have to be honest. I started this book with some pretty high expectations. I was looking for another Beautiful Disaster. But part way through the book i realized I didn't want another BD, not really. I wanted a book that would provoke the same feelings BD did. I can't say this book did that exactly, but it was still a great book. In fact I would have loved it more had I not been comparing it to BD so much I think.<br /><br />OK enough babbling, I loved it. I read reviews before reading it and so some of the mystery that was Jared at the beginning was missing for me. I wished I had gone into this without knowing so much about him. He was pretty awesome though! I love the strong, confident, kick butt males Jamie McGuire creates for her books. She also knows how to write a heart wrenching break up scene. Both books that I have read by her have made me feel like I am part of those break ups. My chest starts hurting and my stomach clenches. If I was the protagonist in either of her stories I wouldn't ahve been able to walk away. No way. I'm weak.<br /><br />Ryan. Lets talk about him. He is the boy Nina was supposed to be with before Jared came into her life. I really liked Ryan. In a way I really wanted him to have his chance with Nina and not in the pretend way. In fact when they were pretending I wanted him to just grab her and kiss her once really good when they were alone, so she could feel what being with Ryan could be like for real. But that definitely would have made life harder on him. Because in the end I still wanted Nina with Jared.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jared showed up a lot in the beginning. He would just pop up when needed. Nina's friends even called him her stalker for a while. I don't understand why Nina didn't just tell her friends that he was a hired body guard basically. Her father had a lot of enemies and Jared has always been there protect her even before she knew him. That would explain his constant presence and how he seemed to know to know so much about her.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br />FAVORITE QUOTES<br /><br />There are so many times I found myself grinning like an idiot while reading this book. I laughed out loud a couple of times too. I just love Jamie McGuire's writing.<br /><br /><br /><br />Kim and I stood, waiting for Beth to gather her miniature office supply store.<br /><br />"This is why I don't bring anything." Kim said, gesturing to Beth.<br /><br />"You borrowed <i>my</i> pen!" Beth objected.<br /><br />"Oh. Right," Kim said, tossing the pen into Beth's bag. "All packed."<br /><br /><br />~Kim and Beth<br /><br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br /><br />"What is that?"<br /><br />Jared sighed. "It's a Vulcan."<br /><br />"Weird. I thought it was a motorcycle." I smiled, but Jared didn't find humor in my words. I put up my hand and separated my fingers into a 'V'. "Live long and... no?"<br /><br /><br />~Nina and Jared<br /><br />BWAHAHAHA Love it!<br /></span>

    <a title="The BookWhisperer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2941466-the-bookwhisperer"><img alt="The BookWhisperer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479666109p2/2941466.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/218131543?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The BookWhisperer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The BookWhisperer" href="/user/show/2941466-the-bookwhisperer">The BookWhisperer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941466-the-bookwhisperer?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218131543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6309335048524889975">Providence was yet another brilliant display of Jamie McGuires raw talent. My first introduce to her works was with the title Beautiful Disaster, and it was a amazing and thrilling story that I have revisited since. McGuire is a amazing author with the ability to combine sweet and simple characters with remarkable story lines. Everytime I have the opportunity to read works by this author I am astounded and awestruck with her ability to create breath taking romances. These are the stories that re</span>
  <span id="freeText6309335048524889975" style="display:none">Providence was yet another brilliant display of Jamie McGuires raw talent. My first introduce to her works was with the title Beautiful Disaster, and it was a amazing and thrilling story that I have revisited since. McGuire is a amazing author with the ability to combine sweet and simple characters with remarkable story lines. Everytime I have the opportunity to read works by this author I am astounded and awestruck with her ability to create breath taking romances. These are the stories that readers will remember long after the last line, and revisit just so that they can feel the emotions of loving the characters all over again. <br /><br />Providence was unique from McGuire's other stories, because of her paranormal twist. This was incredibly benefical to the story at esclating the emotion level even further. As with Beautiful Disaster McGuire is genuinely talented in writing deeply emotional love stories, but when Providence opens the door more a magically connection it seemed to highten the romance even further. (As if I thought that was even possible!) I love feeling as though I am part of the story, and Jamie's ability to absorb readers is clearly evident from this story. The action and suspense promises late night and missed bedtimes. I can't wait to see what the next book will offer. Jamie McGuire is the a amazing author, and something you should not miss! BOOKWHISPERER RECOMMEND!!<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_333901026" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/333901026" />
    <a title="Jessica Buwalda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6926261-jessica-buwalda"><img alt="Jessica Buwalda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600119200p2/6926261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/333901026?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Buwalda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Buwalda" href="/user/show/6926261-jessica-buwalda">Jessica Buwalda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer333901026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5402360771964223643">Alright, so I had high expectations after reading Beautiful Disaster and the book did not fail. The book doesn’t come off the same way as it does through reading the synopsis. Be warned it doesn’t feel like a novel about Heaven and Hell and Demons. No the majority of this novel is a romance. One guy has who has always been around and one girl who never knew it. And the things is you fall in love with Jared from about…well I wouldn’t say the first time you meet him but maybe the second. At first </span>
  <span id="freeText5402360771964223643" style="display:none">Alright, so I had high expectations after reading Beautiful Disaster and the book did not fail. The book doesn’t come off the same way as it does through reading the synopsis. Be warned it doesn’t feel like a novel about Heaven and Hell and Demons. No the majority of this novel is a romance. One guy has who has always been around and one girl who never knew it. And the things is you fall in love with Jared from about…well I wouldn’t say the first time you meet him but maybe the second. At first while I was reading this I thought that they were falling in love all too fast, but when things finally get to be explained then you just seem to understand and if anything you love it even more. This book, like Beautiful Disaster, made me cry, laugh, smile uncontrollably, and some times shakes my head thinking “what the hell are they doing?” But when Jared and Nina go on vacation to the middle of buckshot no where well, I thought it was the most beautiful vacation in the world. The book had my head spinning like her other book and my emotions were all over the place. Is it normal to cry in public while reading? Yes? No? Hmmm…<br />At one point I was scared that the love triangle between Jared, Nina, and Ryan was going to be like the one from Twilight and to be honest I really didn’t want that. Thankfully…it wasn’t. Phew! But no matter what this book is definitely a keep and Jamie McGuire has yet to fail my expectation<br />Good:<br />Nina Grey: She loves her people. And she wants to always take care of them<br />Ryan: By far the sweetest guy in the world. Although he does stupid things sometimes to prove himself.<br />Claire: Claire is like the modern day Nikita. Or Elektra maybe. Or Wonder Woman. <br />Jared: Jared is the sexiest Hybrid. And I imagine him to have the absolute best smile in the world. Even when the guy is stunned happy and they’re mouth is hanging open. Ya even then he would have the big smile I’ve ever seen. He’s tall, he works out, he’s good at what he does, he LOVES Nina, drives a motorcycle, owns his own business, and on top of it all he’s a fantastic dresser. Jamie McGuire posted on her facebook page that Garrett Hedlund would be a good Jared.<br />Oh yes please!<br />Bad: <br />So far I’ve found that the main men in Jamies’ books happen to be very very much in love with the main women in her book. It’s a little scary sometimes and borders on the obsessed level but it always seems to fit and I can’t even get mad at the girls for being in love with them or get mad at the guys either.<br />Overall (Writing style, story line, and general):<br />Overall I did find some of this book a little confusing at time. Only because Jamie doesn’t seem to explain that one second they are in his loft and the next they are at the bank. So it does get a little confusing but then you kind of just figure it out. What I like is how Jamie can get the humour across in her writing and the emotions of the characters. She also really knows how to bring across emotions through the eyes of her characters—literally. Overall, I loved this book and I am happy that I started reading it when the last book finally came out. Because now I can enjoy them all in one week.<br /><br />View more of my review and others at my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.mynotsovacantshelf.blogspot.com">www.mynotsovacantshelf.blogspot.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5402360771964223643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_440298555" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/440298555" />
    <a title="RuthAnn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6000017-ruthann"><img alt="RuthAnn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542508315p2/6000017.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/440298555?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RuthAnn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RuthAnn" href="/user/show/6000017-ruthann">RuthAnn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10289899-providence">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6000017-ruthann?shelf=adulthood">adulthood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6000017-ruthann?shelf=ya-cliche">ya-cliche</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6000017-ruthann?shelf=lendable">lendable</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer440298555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3292468280854346194">So I know that I've lamented a few times that authors keep writing to the same YA formula, and on a few occasions, I've even begged them to stop. But here's the thing--it's like Big Oil. If consumers are going to keep paying money for gasoline (read: same YA shit) then the oil companies are going to keep manufacturing it and not put a lot of time and effort into exploring new sources of renewable energy.<br/><br/>So while I might bitch that Providence had every single YA cliche that I've grown tired of, a</span>
  <span id="freeText3292468280854346194" style="display:none">So I know that I've lamented a few times that authors keep writing to the same YA formula, and on a few occasions, I've even begged them to stop. But here's the thing--it's like Big Oil. If consumers are going to keep paying money for gasoline (read: same YA shit) then the oil companies are going to keep manufacturing it and not put a lot of time and effort into exploring new sources of renewable energy.<br /><br />So while I might bitch that Providence had every single YA cliche that I've grown tired of, authors like Jamie McGuire have no incentive to write different stories because I just paid $9.99 to read the Providence Omnibus. And until readers stop paying money for this, it's going to continue to happen. <br /><br />I've already screwed up, but hopefully, I can stop you from making the same mistake by not giving this book 4 or 5 stars and not writing a review about how romantic it is.<br /><br />It's not that Jamie McGuire is a bad writer; she's not. On the contrary, she is an excellent character builder and storyteller. The part I have a problem with is the plot. It was riddled with the same ever-present storylines as all YA these days, with a few notable exceptions--mainly Maggie Steifvater.<br /><br />Here is a list of my areas of concern:<br /><br />1. The main character is a smart girl. She is a student at Brown for heaven's sake! But her studies get pushed to the side by her inexplicable obsession with someone she doesn't even know.<br /><br />2. A male "protector."<br /><br />3. A male "protector" that is in love with the main character.<br /><br />4. Main character sacrifices herself to protect the protector.<br /><br />5. Flimsy love triangle that is obviously never an issue.<br /><br />6. Characters that are "fated" to be together.<br /><br />7. Characters that are in love after 5 friggin seconds.<br /><br />**<br /><br />I have to give this book 2 stars because McGuire's quality of writing is high, but the story itself gets 1 star. I cannot continue to settle for this tired crap that passes for a good read these days.<br /><br />In the future, I'm going to pay better attention to other people's reviews before I buy, and I would encourage my friends to do the same. It's only when we drive authors/publishers to do something different through economic necessity that better stories will emerge in the marketplace.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3292468280854346194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17201251171955826968" style="display:none">It has been quite long since I read proper YA book and this one was absolutely fantastic! Providence is sweet paranormal story with interesting twists and plenty of action. <br /><br />I was drawn into the story from first chapter and I enjoyed it from the begining to the end. Whole story was beautifully written, gradally building up from chapter to chapter until the very dramatic and cliff-hanging end. <br /><br />The storyline focuses on young woman Nina and mysterious Jared who suddenly enters her life. Jared was absolutely fantastic! Fortunatelly, there were plenty of other characters who helped her to make right final decisions. <br /><br />If you are in mood for some YA paranormal story with perfect male character who is sweet on the one hand and kick-ass character on the other hand, Providence is the best choise for you! <br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kUHzQ2tR25BbBX31I1iCpMuuAS+QnvdnXSd4KIj2ngerZ5qR0A8S+PwuyZTUrYh7HfHm514TeQAGWT6ZRbVsnQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('e+TczZ2NwK6AIfevz9ZOEijpNRpuQm4oFUXsnMy6kGxBwrUfJtMJxicKQ844I0TN/rbS0qDP4E9OO6otAfli9g==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11752803813692237803">Jamie McGuire was born in Tulsa, Oklahoma. She attended Northern Oklahoma College, the University of Central Oklahoma, and Autry Technology Center where she graduated with a degree in Radiography.<br/><br/>Jamie paved the way for the New Adult genre with the international bestseller Beautiful Disaster. Her follow-up novel, Walking Disaster, debuted at #1 on the New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Jou</span>
  <span id="freeText11752803813692237803" style="display:none">Jamie McGuire was born in Tulsa, Oklahoma. She attended Northern Oklahoma College, the University of Central Oklahoma, and Autry Technology Center where she graduated with a degree in Radiography.<br /><br />Jamie paved the way for the New Adult genre with the international bestseller Beautiful Disaster. Her follow-up novel, Walking Disaster, debuted at #1 on the New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal bestseller lists in all four categories. Beautiful Oblivion, book one of the Maddox Brothers series, also topped the New York Times bestseller list, debuting at #1. In 2015, books two and three of the Maddox Brothers series, Beautiful Redemption and Beautiful Sacrifice, respectively, also topped the New York Times, as well as a Beautiful series novella, Something Beautiful. In 2016, Beautiful Burn made an appearance on the New York Times and USA Today, and was also named iBooks' Romance Book of the Year. The same year, A Beautiful Funeral also topped the New York Times bestseller list.<br /><br />Novels also written by Jamie McGuire include: apocalyptic thriller and 2014 UtopYA Best Dystopian Book of the Year, Red Hill; the Providence series, a young adult paranormal romance trilogy; Apolonia, a dark sci-fi romance; and several novellas, including A Beautiful Wedding, Among Monsters, Happenstance: A Novella Series, and Sins of the Innocent.<br /><br />Jamie is the first indie author in history to strike a print deal with retail giant Wal-Mart. Her self-published novel, Beautiful Redemption hit Wal-Mart shelves in September, 2015.<br /><br />Jamie lives in Steamboat Springs, Colorado with her husband, Jeff, and their three children. <br /><br />Find Jamie at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jamiemcguire.com">www.jamiemcguire.com</a> or on Facebook, Twitter, Google +, and Instagram.</span>
